<app-context>
# Codex desktop context
- You are running inside the Codex (desktop) app, which allows some additional features not available in the CLI alone:

### Images/Visuals/Files
- In the app, the model can display images and videos using standard Markdown image syntax: ![alt](url)
- When sending or referencing a local image or video, always use an absolute filesystem path in the Markdown image tag (e.g., ![alt](/absolute/path.png)); relative paths and plain text will not render the media.
- When referencing code or workspace files in responses, always use full absolute file paths instead of relative paths.
- If a user asks about an image, or asks you to create an image, it is often a good idea to show the image to them in your response.
- Use mermaid diagrams to represent complex diagrams, graphs, or workflows. Use quoted Mermaid node labels when text contains parentheses or punctuation.
- Return web URLs as Markdown links (e.g., [label](https://example.com)).

### Workspace Dependencies
- For sheets, slides, and documents, call `load_workspace_dependencies` to find the bundled runtime and libraries.

### Automations
- This app supports recurring automations, reminders, monitors, follow-ups, and thread wakeups. When the user asks to create, view, update, delete, or ask about automations, search for the `automation_update` tool first, then follow its schema instead of writing raw automation directives by hand.
- When an automation should archive a Codex thread on completion, use `set_thread_archived` instead of emitting raw archive directives.

### Thread Coordination
- When the user asks to create, fork, inspect, continue, hand off, pin, archive, rename, or otherwise manage Codex threads, search for the relevant thread tool first: `create_thread`, `fork_thread`, `list_threads`, `read_thread`, `send_message_to_thread`, `handoff_thread`, `set_thread_pinned`, `set_thread_archived`, or `set_thread_title`.
- Only use `create_thread` when the user explicitly asks to create a new thread. Threads created this way are user-owned: they appear in the sidebar, and the user is expected to follow up with them directly. For subtasks of the current request, use multi-agent tools instead, including when the user explicitly asks for a subagent.
- After a successful `create_thread` call, emit `::created-thread{threadId="..."}` for a created thread or `::created-thread{pendingWorktreeId="..."}` for queued worktree setup on its own line in your final response.

### Inline Code Comments
- Use the ::code-comment{...} directive when you need to attach feedback directly to specific code lines.
- Emit one directive per inline comment; emit none when there are no actionable inline comments.
- Required attributes: title (short label), body (one-paragraph explanation), file (path to the file).
- Optional attributes: start, end (1-based line numbers), priority (0-3).
- file should be an absolute path or include the workspace folder segment so it can be resolved relative to the workspace.
- Keep line ranges tight; end defaults to start.
- Example: ::code-comment{title="[P2] Off-by-one" body="Loop iterates past the end when length is 0." file="/path/to/foo.ts" start=10 end=11 priority=2}

### Git
- Branch prefix: `codex/`. Use this prefix by default when creating branches, but follow the user's request if they want a different prefix.
- After successfully staging files, emit `::git-stage{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line in your final response.
- After successfully creating a commit, emit `::git-commit{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line in your final response.
- After successfully creating or switching the thread onto a branch, emit `::git-create-branch{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line in your final response.
- After successfully pushing the current branch, emit `::git-push{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line in your final response.
- After successfully creating a pull request, emit `::git-create-pr{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name" url="https://..." isDraft=true}` on its own line in your final response. Include `isDraft=false` for ready PRs.
- Only emit these git directives in your final response after the action actually succeeds, never in commentary updates. Keep attributes single-line.
</app-context>

### How to use skills
- Discovery: The list above is the skills available in this session (name + description + short path). Skill bodies live on disk at the listed paths after expanding the matching alias from `### Skill roots`.
- Trigger rules: If the user names a skill (with `$SkillName` or plain text) OR the task clearly matches a skill's description shown above, you must use that skill for that turn. Multiple mentions mean use them all. Do not carry skills across turns unless re-mentioned.
- Missing/blocked: If a named skill isn't in the list or the path can't be read, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
- How to use a skill (progressive disclosure):
  1) After deciding to use a skill, the main agent must expand the listed short `path` with the matching alias from `### Skill roots`, then open and read its `SKILL.md` completely before taking task actions. If a read is truncated or paginated, continue until EOF.
  2) When `SKILL.md` references relative paths (e.g., `scripts/foo.py`), resolve them relative to the directory containing that expanded `SKILL.md` first, and only consider other paths if needed.
  3) If `SKILL.md` points to extra folders such as `references/`, use its routing instructions to identify the files required for the task. The main agent must read each required instruction or reference file itself before acting on it. Do not delegate reading, summarizing, or interpreting skill instructions to a subagent. Subagents may still perform task work when the selected skill allows it.
  4) If `scripts/` exist, prefer running or patching them instead of retyping large code blocks.
  5) If `assets/` or templates exist, reuse them instead of recreating from scratch.
- Coordination and sequencing:
  - If multiple skills apply, choose the minimal set that covers the request and state the order you'll use them.
  - Announce which skill(s) you're using and why (one short line). If you skip an obvious skill, say why.
- Context hygiene:
  - Progressive disclosure applies to selecting relevant files, not partially reading a selected instruction file. Do not load unrelated references, scripts, or assets.
  - Avoid deep reference-chasing: prefer opening only files directly linked from `SKILL.md` unless you're blocked.
  - When variants exist (frameworks, providers, domains), pick only the relevant reference file(s) and note that choice.
- Safety and fallback: If a skill can't be applied cleanly (missing files, unclear instructions), state the issue, pick the next-best approach, and continue.
</skills_instructions>

## Plugins
A plugin is a local bundle of skills, MCP servers, and apps.
### How to use plugins
- Skill naming: If a plugin contributes skills, those skill entries are prefixed with `plugin_name:` in the Skills list.
- MCP naming: Plugin-provided MCP tools keep standard MCP identifiers such as `mcp__server__tool`; use tool provenance to tell which plugin they come from.
- Trigger rules: If the user explicitly names a plugin, prefer capabilities associated with that plugin for that turn.
- Relationship to capabilities: Plugins are not invoked directly. Use their underlying skills, MCP tools, and app tools to help solve the task.
- Relevance: Determine what a plugin can help with from explicit user mention or from the plugin-associated skills, MCP tools, and apps exposed elsewhere in this turn.
- Missing/blocked: If the user requests a plugin that does not have relevant callable capabilities for the task, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
</plugins_instructions>
## Memory

You have access to a memory folder with guidance from prior runs. It can save
time and help you stay consistent. Use it whenever it is likely to help.

Decision boundary: should you use memory for a new user query?

- Skip memory ONLY when the request is clearly self-contained and does not need
  workspace history, conventions, or prior decisions.
- Hard skip examples: current time/date, simple translation, simple sentence
  rewrite, one-line shell command, trivial formatting.
- Use memory by default when ANY of these are true:
  - the query mentions workspace/repo/module/path/files in MEMORY_SUMMARY below,
  - the user asks for prior context / consistency / previous decisions,
  - the task is ambiguous and could depend on earlier project choices,
  - the ask is a non-trivial and related to MEMORY_SUMMARY below.
- If unsure, do a quick memory pass.

Memory layout (general -> specific):

- C:\Users\t250c\.codex\memories/memory_summary.md (already provided below; do NOT open again)
- C:\Users\t250c\.codex\memories/MEMORY.md (searchable registry; primary file to query)
- C:\Users\t250c\.codex\memories/skills/<skill-name>/ (skill folder)
  - SKILL.md (entrypoint instructions)
  - scripts/ (optional helper scripts)
  - examples/ (optional example outputs)
  - templates/ (optional templates)
- C:\Users\t250c\.codex\memories/rollout_summaries/ (per-rollout recaps + evidence snippets)
  - The paths of these entries can be found in C:\Users\t250c\.codex\memories/MEMORY.md or C:\Users\t250c\.codex\memories/rollout_summaries/ as `rollout_path`
  - These files are append-only `jsonl`: `session_meta.payload.id` identifies the session, `turn_context` marks turn boundaries, `event_msg` is the lightweight status stream, and `response_item` contains actual messages, tool calls, and tool outputs.
  - For efficient lookup, prefer matching the filename suffix or `session_meta.payload.id`; avoid broad full-content scans unless needed.

Quick memory pass (when applicable):

1. Skim the MEMORY_SUMMARY below and extract task-relevant keywords.
2. Search C:\Users\t250c\.codex\memories/MEMORY.md using those keywords.
3. Only if MEMORY.md directly points to rollout summaries/skills, open the 1-2
   most relevant files under C:\Users\t250c\.codex\memories/rollout_summaries/ or
   C:\Users\t250c\.codex\memories/skills/.
4. If above are not clear and you need exact commands, error text, or precise evidence, search over `rollout_path` for more evidence.
5. If there are no relevant hits, stop memory lookup and continue normally.

Quick-pass budget:

- Keep memory lookup lightweight: ideally <= 4-6 search steps before main work.
- Avoid broad scans of all rollout summaries.

During execution: if you hit repeated errors, confusing behavior, or suspect
relevant prior context, redo the quick memory pass.

How to decide whether to verify memory:

- Consider both risk of drift and verification effort.
- If a fact is likely to drift and is cheap to verify, verify it before
  answering.
- If a fact is likely to drift but verification is expensive, slow, or
  disruptive, it is acceptable to answer from memory in an interactive turn,
  but you should say that it is memory-derived, note that it may be stale, and
  consider offering to refresh it live.
- If a fact is lower-drift and expensive to verify, it is usually fine to
  answer from memory directly.

When answering from memory without current verification:

- If you rely on memory for a fact that you did not verify in the current turn,
  say so briefly in the final answer.
- If that fact is plausibly drift-prone or comes from an older note, older
  snapshot, or prior run summary, say that it may be stale or outdated.
- If live verification was skipped and a refresh would be useful in the
  interactive context, consider offering to verify or refresh it live.
- Do not present unverified memory-derived facts as confirmed-current.
- Prefer a short refresh offer for interactive questions, especially about prior
  results, commands, timing, or older snapshots.

Memory citation requirements:

- If ANY relevant memory files were used: append exactly one
`<oai-mem-citation>` block as the VERY LAST content of the final reply.
  Normal responses should include the answer first, then append the
`<oai-mem-citation>` block at the end.
- Use this exact structure for programmatic parsing:
```
<oai-mem-citation>
<citation_entries>
MEMORY.md:234-236|note=[responsesapi citation extraction code pointer]
rollout_summaries/2026-02-17T21-23-02-LN3m-example.md:10-12|note=[weekly report format]
</citation_entries>
<rollout_ids>
019c6e27-e55b-73d1-87d8-4e01f1f75043
019c7714-3b77-74d1-9866-e1f484aae2ab
</rollout_ids>
</oai-mem-citation>
```
- `citation_entries` is for rendering:
  - one citation entry per line
  - format: `<file>:<line_start>-<line_end>|note=[<how memory was used>]`
  - use file paths relative to the memory base path (for example, `MEMORY.md`,
    `rollout_summaries/...`, `skills/...`)
  - only cite files actually used under the memory base path (do not cite
    workspace files as memory citations)
  - if you used `MEMORY.md` and then a rollout summary/skill file, cite both
  - list entries in order of importance (most important first)
  - `note` should be short, single-line, and use simple characters only (avoid
    unusual symbols, no newlines)
- `rollout_ids` is for us to track what previous rollouts you find useful:
  - include one rollout id per line
  - rollout ids should look like UUIDs (for example,
    `019c6e27-e55b-73d1-87d8-4e01f1f75043`)
  - include unique ids only; do not repeat ids
  - an empty `<rollout_ids>` section is allowed if no rollout ids are available
  - you can find rollout ids in rollout summary files and MEMORY.md
  - do not include file paths or notes in this section
  - For every `citation_entries`, try to find and cite the corresponding rollout id if possible
- Never include memory citations inside pull-request messages.
- Never cite blank lines; double-check ranges.

Updating memories:

You can update the memories **only** when explicitly asked by the user. This must always come from a direct request from the user.
- Write your update in C:\Users\t250c\.codex\memories/extensions/ad_hoc/notes/
- Each update must be one small file containing what you want to add/delete/update from the memories.
- The name of this file must be `<timestamp>-<short slug>.md`
- Do not try to edit the memory files yourself, only add one update note in C:\Users\t250c\.codex\memories/extensions/ad_hoc/notes/

## User Profile
The user works with Codex on Windows across recurring lanes: embedded/Keil firmware diagnosis for industrial machines, CAN/protocol-sheet and HTML protocol documentation work, Qt upper-computer tooling, MCGS scripts, local Windows troubleshooting, and Codex continuity/history repair. They expect the agent to recover prior context from local memory, rollout artifacts, or toolkit mirrors before asking them to restate it.

They prefer concrete, source-backed outputs: exact paths, exact files, exact values, runnable local fallbacks, and deliverables they can open or use immediately. For embedded diagnosis they usually want read-only tracing through the live checkout unless they explicitly ask for edits. When they say something should be remembered globally, they expect the reusable rule or workflow to be persisted.

When they point at a specific local path, file, or package, inspect the real target immediately. When they distinguish a third-party package from their own project, keep those codebases separate while still extracting reusable clues. On Windows troubleshooting or scripting tasks, they often want the agent to finish the real local task, not stop at explanation.

### user 2026-06-28T16:57:47.533Z

```text
0x154 要变成稳定高频发送，不能只在 P07/P10 页面优先发 这个是什么意思？
```

### assistant 2026-06-28T16:58:09.886Z

```text
意思是：

`0x154` 现在承担的是“关节/编码器实际值”发给 QT，比如三臂的根摆、底座、推进梁、D1/E1/F、CD、GG1 等。它不是最终 H 点坐标，而是 QT 如果想自己算正解、算 H 点时需要的输入数据。

现在的问题是：`0x154` 目前属于 **P07/P10 页面优先数据**。也就是说，QT 进入调试/标定相关页面时，算法 PCB 才会重点发这些关节值；如果 QT 在主界面、数据监测界面或别的页面，`0x154` 可能不发，或者发得很慢。

我说“`0x154` 要变成稳定高频发送”，意思是：

1. `0x154` 不应该跟页面绑定。
2. 不管 QT 当前在哪个页面，算法 PCB 都应该按固定周期发送 `0x154`。
3. QT 不能因为切换页面就丢掉关节角度数据。
4. 如果以后 H 点坐标放到 QT 端计算，`0x154` 就必须是基础实时数据流。

比如现在逻辑类似：

```text
P07/P10 页面：优先发 0x154
其他页面：0x154 不一定发，或者低频发
```

我建议如果 QT 要参与正解计算，应改成：

```text
任何页面：
  固定周期发 0x153 深度
  固定周期发 0x154 关节/编码器值
  固定周期发 0x15A 离线状态
  需要时再发 0x150 / 0x152 作为算法 PCB 计算结果
```

关键点是：  
如果 H 点还是算法 PCB 算，QT 只显示 `0x150`，那 `0x154` 慢一点没关系。  
但如果你想让 QT 自己算 H 点，`0x154` 就不能只在 P07/P10 页面才重点发，必须稳定、高频、全局发送。
```

### user 2026-06-28T16:59:16.039Z

```text
那也是P10不是P7啊。
```

### assistant 2026-06-28T16:59:33.569Z

```text
对，应该是 **P10，不是 P7**。

我前面把 `P07/P10` 写在一起不严谨。准确说：

`0x154` 是 **编码器/关节实际值调试数据**，页面归属应该是 **P10 调试/关节数据界面**。  
`P7` 不应该作为 `0x154` 的优先发送条件。

真正要分两种情况：

```text
如果 H 点继续由算法 PCB 算：
  0x154 只在 P10 高频发即可，其他页面低频或不发都可以。

如果以后 QT 自己算 H 点：
  0x154 就不能只依赖 P10 页面，必须变成后台稳定高频发送。
```

所以协议里应该写清楚：  
**当前显示调试用途：0x154 属于 P10。**  
**若 QT 端接管正解/H 点计算：0x154 升级为全局基础实时数据，不再绑定 P10。**
```

### user 2026-06-28T17:00:40.641Z

```text
0x150 呢？
```

### assistant 2026-06-28T17:01:01.585Z

```text
`0x150` 跟 `0x154` 不一样。

`0x150` 应该是 **算法 PCB 算完后的最终 H 点坐标**，也就是 QT 直接显示/使用的结果数据。它不应该归到 P10 调试页面里。

当前建议：

```text
0x150 = 三臂 H 点坐标，快速数据
0x154 = 编码器/关节实际值，P10 调试数据
```

`0x150` 内容应该是：

```text
B0 = 0x10 左臂 H 点
B0 = 0x20 中臂 H 点
B0 = 0x30 右臂 H 点

B1-B2 = H.x，int16，小端，单位 mm
B3-B4 = H.y，int16，小端，单位 mm
B5-B6 = H.z，int16，小端，单位 mm
B7 = 有效标志，1 有效，0 无效
```

注意：这里不要再搞 `×100`。你前面判断是对的，H 点坐标用 **mm 级精度**够了。否则 X/Y/Z 三个坐标放不下，还会拖慢协议。

发送策略建议：

```text
0x150：快速发，页面需要 H 点时必须优先发
0x152：推进梁 XZ/YZ 面夹角，快速发
0x153：实时凿岩深度，快速发
0x154：编码器角度组，P10 调试时高频，其他页面可慢
0x15A：离线/状态，慢一点可以
```

所以结论是：

`0x150` 不是 P10 专属，它是核心实时业务数据。  
只要 QT 当前页面需要显示末端点/H 点坐标，算法 PCB 就应该稳定发送 `0x150`。  
如果未来改成 QT 自己算 H 点，那 `0x150` 可以降级为算法 PCB 的对比/调试结果；但在当前方案里，`0x150` 仍然是 QT 使用 H 点坐标的主数据。
```

### user 2026-06-28T17:01:13.122Z

```text
哦。明白了。
```

### assistant 2026-06-28T17:01:17.916Z

```text
对，就是这个分工：

`0x150` 是算法 PCB 给 QT 的最终 H 点结果，属于快速业务数据。  
`0x154` 是关节/编码器中间量，当前主要给 P10 调试看。  

只有当以后决定让 QT 自己算 H 点时，`0x154` 才需要从“P10 调试数据”升级成“全局高频基础数据”。
```

### user 2026-06-28T17:02:46.822Z

```text
我现在是想把算法PCB的功能 复制一份到QT端。这样两者算出来的结果，我可以进行对比。做到一个冗余的效果。如果把H点计算结果放到QT，避免Q点数据导来导去。  但是目前还是两者兼有。
```

### assistant 2026-06-28T17:03:00.157Z

```text
我先把这个目标按工程方案拆开：你现在不是要立刻替代算法 PCB，而是要让 QT 并行复算一份，拿 QT_H 和 PCB_H 做差值对比。这个方案成立，但协议上必须补齐“QT 复算所需输入”和“参数一致性”。
```

### assistant 2026-06-28T17:03:23.927Z

```text
这个思路是对的：现在目标不是删掉算法 PCB 的 H 点计算，而是 **算法 PCB 算一份，QT 端复制算法再算一份，两边对比**。

工程上我建议这样定：

```text
算法 PCB：
  继续算 H 点
  继续发 0x150，作为 PCB_H

QT：
  接收关节/编码器数据
  接收车体倾角 0x28F 对应数据
  用同一套参数再算一遍 H 点，作为 QT_H
  页面上显示 PCB_H、QT_H、差值
```

关键是，QT 要复算 H 点，光有 `0x150` 不够。`0x150` 已经是结果。QT 需要的是输入量：

```text
0x154：三臂关节/编码器实际值
新增建议 0x155：车体倾角 roll / pitch，也就是算法 PCB 当前用的 0x28F 数据
0x153：实时凿岩深度，单独显示或参与孔深逻辑
参数：零点、机械尺寸、机械误差拟合参数、Q_body/Q_world 或最终 R/T 坐标转换参数
```

所以协议上要改的核心不是 `0x150`，而是：

1. `0x150` 保留  
   仍然是算法 PCB 发给 QT 的 H 点结果。

2. `0x154` 要稳定发  
   如果 QT 要实时复算，就不能只在 P10 页面才发。否则 QT 在其他页面没有足够输入，算不出来或延迟很大。

3. 需要补一个倾角数据 ID  
   现在缺的是 `0x28F` 对应的车体 roll / pitch。可以新增 `0x155` 发给 QT。

4. 参数要统一版本  
   两边都算 H 点，就必须保证 QT 和算法 PCB 用的是同一套零点、拟合参数、Q 点坐标转换参数。建议 QT 做参数主站，算法 PCB 保存最终参数，并加一个参数版本号/CRC，防止两边参数不一致还在对比。

关于你说的“避免 Q 点数据导来导去”，这里要分清：

```text
如果只有 QT 算 H 点：
  Q 点数据只放 QT，算法 PCB 不需要完整 Q 点数据。

如果 QT 和算法 PCB 都同时算：
  算法 PCB 仍然需要最终坐标转换参数。
  但不一定要导全部历史 Q 点，只需要导最终 R/T、倾角零点、机械误差修正参数。
```

也就是说，后续最合理的结构是：

```text
QT 管理 Q 点、拟合样本、参数版本
QT 下发最终参数给算法 PCB
算法 PCB 用最终参数继续算 PCB_H
QT 本地用同一参数算 QT_H
两边结果做差值对比
```

显示上建议加：

```text
左臂：PCB_H / QT_H / ΔX / ΔY / ΔZ / 误差长度
中臂：PCB_H / QT_H / ΔX / ΔY / ΔZ / 误差长度
右臂：PCB_H / QT_H / ΔX / ΔY / ΔZ / 误差长度
```

误差长度：

```text
err = sqrt(ΔX² + ΔY² + ΔZ²)
```

这样你可以先验证 QT 复制算法是否一致。验证稳定以后，再决定是否让 QT 的 H 点成为主结果。
```

```

### assistant 2026-06-28T17:05:57.485Z

```text
已经核到两个关键信息：当前文档把 `0x15A` 定义成“掉线位图”，代码里也是每 100ms 左右发 `B0~B3` 掉线位。下一步我看一下 `B4~B7` 有没有被占用，决定能不能直接放倾角。
```

### assistant 2026-06-28T17:06:33.423Z

```text
`B4~B7` 现在确实是空的：固件发送前直接置 0，文档也写 Qt 不做业务解析。也就是说，把倾角塞进 `0x15A` 从字节空间上可行，最好明确成“掉线位 + 倾角数据”的组合帧。
```

### assistant 2026-06-28T17:07:01.658Z

```text
目前 `0x15A` 是 **算法 PCB -> QT 的掉线位图帧**，不是角度数据帧。

当前定义是：

```text
0x15A

B0：
  b0 左臂 root 掉线
  b1 左臂 base 掉线
  b2 左臂 boom 掉线
  b3 左臂 d1 掉线
  b4 左臂 e1 掉线
  b5 左臂 f 掉线
  b6 左臂 cd 掉线
  b7 左臂 gg1 掉线

B1：
  b0 左臂深度 掉线
  b1~b7 中臂 base/boom/d1/e1/f/cd/gg1 掉线

B2：
  b0 中臂深度 掉线
  b1~b7 右臂 root/base/boom/d1/e1/f/cd 掉线

B3：
  b0 右臂 gg1 掉线
  b1 右臂深度 掉线
  b2 算法 PCB 掉线
  b3 倾角传感器 0x28F 掉线
  b4~b7 保留

B4~B7：
  当前保留，程序固定发 0
```

我看了代码，[App_usr.c](<E:/AI_划时代/全电脑_算法PCB/正确资料_算法PCB_CAN协议/MC_LCD - 7Control_V1.2/Src/App_usr.c:1165>) 里面现在确实是：

```c
CAN_SBuf2[0] = 掉线位B0;
CAN_SBuf2[1] = 掉线位B1;
CAN_SBuf2[2] = 掉线位B2;
CAN_SBuf2[3] = 掉线位B3;
CAN_SBuf2[4] = 0;
CAN_SBuf2[5] = 0;
CAN_SBuf2[6] = 0;
CAN_SBuf2[7] = 0;
```

所以你想把 `roll / pitch` 放到 `0x15A`，空间上是可以的，最合适就是：

```text
B4-B5 = 0x28F roll_raw，uint16，小端
B6-B7 = 0x28F pitch_raw，uint16，小端
```

我建议放 **原始 raw16**，不要放 `角度*100`。原因是算法 PCB 当前读取 `0x28F` 后是这样处理的：

```text
roll_raw  = 0x28F B0-B1
pitch_raw = 0x28F B2-B3

角度 = raw * 360 / 65535
```

如果 QT 要复制算法 PCB 的计算，QT 收 `raw16` 最干净，直接用同一个换算公式。  
如果发 `角度*100`，0~360 度会到 36000，超过 signed int16 的 32767，容易出坑。

结论：  
`0x15A` 现在是掉线帧，`B4~B7` 空着。可以改成：

```text
0x15A = 掉线位 + 车体倾角原始值
B0-B3 掉线位保持不变
B4-B5 roll_raw
B6-B7 pitch_raw
```

这样 QT 既能看掉线状态，又能拿到复算 H 点需要的车体倾角输入。
```

### user 2026-06-28T17:07:57.620Z

```text
现在28F是怎么解析数据的？
```

### assistant 2026-06-28T17:08:21.994Z

```text
我按嵌入式 CAN 解析来核当前源码，重点看 `0x28F` 的字节序、换算公式、掉线判定，以及它后续进入算法时是否再标零/缩放。
```

### assistant 2026-06-28T17:08:50.860Z

```text
现在算法 PCB 对 `0x28F` 的解析是这样的：

```text
CAN ID: 0x28F

B0-B1 = roll_raw，uint16，小端
B2-B3 = pitch_raw，uint16，小端
B4-B7 = 当前代码未解析
```

代码位置：[App_usr.c](<E:/AI_划时代/全电脑_算法PCB/正确资料_算法PCB_CAN协议/MC_LCD - 7Control_V1.2/Src/App_usr.c:1058>)

当前解析逻辑：

```c
rdCan = CAN1_Get_Data(0x28F);
if((rdCan == 0xFF) || (rdCan == 0xEE))
{
    return;
}

roll_raw  = CAN1_RBuf[0] + (CAN1_RBuf[1] << 8);
pitch_raw = CAN1_RBuf[2] + (CAN1_RBuf[3] << 8);

body_roll_raw  = roll_raw  * 360.0f / 65535.0f;
body_pitch_raw = pitch_raw * 360.0f / 65535.0f;
```

也就是说，`0x28F` 原始值是 **0~65535 对应 0~360 度**。

注意一个细节：代码里的变量名叫 `body_roll_raw`、`body_pitch_raw`，但它们保存的已经不是 CAN 原始 raw16，而是 **换算后的角度值 deg**。

后续进入算法时又会做标零和方向/比例处理：

```text
body_roll_deg  = (body_roll_raw  - body_roll_zero_raw)  * scale * sign
body_pitch_deg = (body_pitch_raw - body_pitch_zero_raw) * scale * sign
```

代码位置：[Arm200A_Kine.c](<E:/AI_划时代/全电脑_算法PCB/正确资料_算法PCB_CAN协议/MC_LCD - 7Control_V1.2/Src/Arm200A_Kine.c:1138>)

然后在坐标变换里用增量倾角补偿：

```text
roll_delta  = body_roll_deg  - tilt_roll_zero_deg
pitch_delta = body_pitch_deg - tilt_pitch_zero_deg
```

代码位置：[Arm200A_Kine.c](<E:/AI_划时代/全电脑_算法PCB/正确资料_算法PCB_CAN协议/MC_LCD - 7Control_V1.2/Src/Arm200A_Kine.c:1207>)

掉线方面，`0x28F` 注册了超时：

```text
RegisterID(0x28F, ..., 1000)
```

代码位置：[CanOpen.c](<E:/AI_划时代/全电脑_算法PCB/正确资料_算法PCB_CAN协议/MC_LCD - 7Control_V1.2/Src/CanOpen.c:321>)

如果 `0x28F` 掉线，当前 `0x15A/B3.b3` 会置 1：

```text
0x15A B3.b3 = 倾角传感器 0x28F 掉线
```

所以如果你要把 `0x28F` 放进 `0x15A` 给 QT，我建议保持：

```text
0x15A B4-B5 = roll_raw 原始 uint16 小端
0x15A B6-B7 = pitch_raw 原始 uint16 小端
```

QT 端再按同样公式算：

```text
angle_deg = raw16 * 360.0 / 65535.0
```
```

### user 2026-06-28T17:09:47.463Z

```text
反正跟28F处理一样即可
```

### assistant 2026-06-28T17:10:01.455Z

```text
明白，口径就按“`0x15A` 后 4 字节原样透传 `0x28F` 前 4 字节”定，不再二次定义单位。这样 QT 和算法 PCB 用同一套解析公式，后面对比结果不会因为协议换算不同引入偏差。
```

### assistant 2026-06-28T17:10:20.469Z

```text
可以，就按这个定：

```text
0x15A B4-B7 完全等价于 0x28F B0-B3

B4-B5 = roll_raw，uint16，小端
B6-B7 = pitch_raw，uint16，小端
```

QT 端解析方式和算法 PCB 当前处理 `0x28F` 一样：

```text
roll_deg  = roll_raw  * 360.0 / 65535.0
pitch_deg = pitch_raw * 360.0 / 65535.0
```

不要用 `角度*100`，也不要 signed int16。  
`0x15A/B0-B3` 继续保留掉线位，`B3.b3` 还是 `0x28F` 倾角传感器掉线标志。

后面协议就写成：

```text
0x15A = 编码器/倾角掉线位 + 0x28F 倾角原始值透传
```

这样 QT 复算 H 点时，倾角输入和算法 PCB 完全同源、同格式。

### assistant 2026-06-29T00:45:59.274Z

```text

### assistant 2026-06-29T00:46:39.045Z

```text

### assistant 2026-06-29T01:01:31.351Z

```text
拟合结果不是一两个值，而是 `ARM200A_FIX_NUM=22` 个补偿标量。我再把 22 个标量的映射读出来，这样回答能说清楚“数值是什么、Qt 现在有没有保存”。
```

### assistant 2026-06-29T01:01:55.169Z

```text
现在 Qt 对“拟合数值”的处理还不完整。

当前实际逻辑是：

1. 点“记录样本”时  
   Qt 把当前 0x154/0x15A 输入快照 + 实测 H 点写进本机算法的 A2 样本池。

2. 点“拟合完成”时  
   Qt 调 `Arm200A_FitLeft/Mid/Right()`，本机算法会算出 22 个补偿量，写到：
   - `gArmLeftFix`
   - `gArmMidFix`
   - `gArmRightFix`

3. 后续 Qt 自己算 H 点时  
   会直接使用这些 `gArm*Fix` 补偿量，所以运行时是生效的。

但是目前缺的地方是：

- Qt 没有把这 22 个拟合数值显示出来。
- Qt 没有把这 22 个拟合数值保存到本机配置。
- Qt 关闭后，本机 `gArm*Fix` 会丢。
- Qt 没有从算法 PCB 读取 PCB 端最终拟合值。
- 当前协议 0x150/E0/E1 只反馈状态、点数、误差、RMS，不反馈 22 个补偿值。

这 22 个值的映射是：

`0..21 = o0o1.y, o0o1.z, o1o.x, o1o.y, o1o.z, ob.x, ob.z, ba.x, ac.x, ac.z, d1e.x, d1e.y, ee1.y, e1f.x, e1f.y, fg.x, fg.y, fg.z, g1h.x, g1h.z, dd1_mm, e1e2.z`

所以结论：Qt 现在只是“临时算出来并运行时使用”，还没有做“拟合结果管理”。

我建议下一步补三件事：
1. Qt 拟合完成后，把 22 个 `fix` 数值读出来显示。
2. 保存到 Qt 本机配置，下次启动自动恢复进 `gArm*Fix`。
3. 协议里如果你想对比算法 PCB 和 Qt 的拟合结果，需要新增 PCB 端 22 个 `fix` 结果反馈帧。
```

### user 2026-06-29T01:02:56.680Z

```text
拟合就是为了修正H点误差的，不能每次都进去拟合，会拖慢软件的。必须保存下来，算法PCB好也是这么干的啊。你查下。
```
